## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time and concentration, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on concentration raised to some power (reaction order), with possible time-dependent effects from complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + A) (transition between reaction orders)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (photolysis or time-varying conditions)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Damped oscillatory rate: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * t (concentration and time coupled effect)
- Square-root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (diffusion-limited surface reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed bimolecular reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer or half-integer reaction orders → Power-law rate expressions A**n where n = 0, 0.5, 1, 2, 3 reflect elementary step molecularity
- Equilibrium approach → Linear terms with offsets (c0*A + c1) indicate reversible reactions approaching equilibrium concentration
- Saturation in rate vs concentration → Rational forms A/(c+A) indicate enzyme/catalyst site saturation (Michaelis-Menten mechanism)
- Product of concentration and complement → A*(c-A) form indicates autocatalytic or logistic growth where product catalyzes its own formation
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → Multiplicative t-dependent factors suggest non-autonomous systems like varying temperature, light intensity, or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of power-law terms → Multiple additive A**n terms suggest parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Rational functions with powers in denominator → (A**n)/(c+A**m) suggest cooperative or inhibitory binding mechanisms
- Negative fractional exponents → A**(-c) terms can arise from complex chain reaction mechanisms with termination steps
- Square root concentration dependence → A**0.5 commonly arises from dissociation equilibria or radical chain initiation steps
- Polynomial rate expressions → Higher-order polynomials in A often result from quasi-steady-state approximation of multi-step mechanisms
